data-file-width="38" data-file-height="59" /></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 69px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px; background-color: #FFFFF6;"></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 69px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/31px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png" width="31" height="59" equipment">kit</a></b>\n</p>\n</div></td><td><div style="width: 100px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0; text-align: center;">\n<div style="position: relative; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 100px; height: 135px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;">\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px; background-color: #00CC62;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kit_left_arm_navyborder.png" class="image"><img alt="Kit left arm navyborder.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/18/Kit_left_arm_navyborder.png" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></a></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kit_left_arm.svg/47px-Kit_left_arm.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kit_left_arm.svg/62px-Kit_left_arm.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 31px; top: 0px; width: 38px; height: 59px; background-color: #00CC62;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e5/Kit_body_navycollar.png" width="38" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="38" data-file-height="59" /></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 31px; top: 0px; width: 38px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kit_body.svg/57px-Kit_body.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kit_body.svg/76px-Kit_body.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="38" data-file-height="59" /></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 69px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px; background-color: #00CC62;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kit_right_arm_navyborder.png" class="image"><img alt="Kit right arm navyborder.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/Kit_right_arm_navyborder.png" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></a></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 69px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/31px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/47px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/62px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></div>\n<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 80px; background-color: #00CC62;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/Kit_trousers_long.png" width="100" height="80" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="80" /></div>\n</div>\n<p><b>ODI <a href="/wiki/Cricket_clothing_and_equipment" title="Cricket clothing and equipment">kit</a></b>\n</p>\n</div></td></tr>\n</tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<i>As of 31 August 2018</i></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Ireland cricket team</b> represents <a href="/wiki/All-Ireland" title="All-Ireland">all of Ireland</a>. They participate in <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">ODI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> matches at international level. They are the 11th <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members#Full_Members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">Full Member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> (ICC), having been awarded <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket#Test_status" title="Test cricket">Test status</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_cricket_team" title="Afghanistan national cricket team">Afghanistan</a>, on 22 June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ireland are ranked 12th in <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> (ODI) cricket. Ireland played their first ODI in 2006 against <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a>. Since then, they have gone on to play 137&#160;ODIs, resulting in 60&#160;victories, 67&#160;defeats, 7&#160;<a href="/wiki/Result_(cricket)#No_result" title="Result (cricket)">no results</a>, and 3&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tie_(draw)" title="Tie (draw)">ties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-odiresults_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odiresults-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Contracts for players were introduced in 2009, marking the transition to becoming a professional team. <a href="/wiki/Cricket_Ireland" title="Cricket Ireland">Cricket Ireland</a> is the sport\'s governing body in Ireland.\n</p><p>Cricket was introduced to Ireland in the 19th century, and the first match played by an Ireland team was in 1855. Ireland toured Canada and the United States in the late 19th century, and occasionally hosted matches against touring sides. Rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_cricket_team" title="Scotland national cricket team">Scotland national cricket team</a> was established when the teams first played each other in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Ireland\'s maiden <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class</a> match was played in 1902.\n</p><p>In 1993 the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Cricket_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Cricket Union">Irish Cricket Union</a>, the predecessor to Cricket Ireland, was elected to the ICC as an Associate member. Associates are the next level of team below those that play Test cricket. Due to their successes in the Intercontinental Cup and at the World Cup, they were labelled the "leading Associate"<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and stated their intention to become a full member by 2020. This intention was realised in June 2017, when the ICC unanimously decided to award Ireland and Afghanistan full Test status, which allows them to participate in Test matches.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ireland qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Ireland_at_the_Cricket_World_Cup" title="Ireland at the Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> for the first time in 2007, and has since played in the 2011 and 2015 tournaments. They also qualified for the 2009, 2010, 2012, and 2014 <a href="/wiki/ICC_World_Twenty20" title="ICC World Twenty20">World Twenty20</a> competitions. Ireland also play international cricket in the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="ICC Intercontinental Cup">ICC Intercontinental Cup</a>, which they have won four times since 2005, including the most recent competition in 2013.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Personnel</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Playing_staff"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">First-class</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cricket was introduced to Ireland by the English in the towns of <a href="/wiki/Kilkenny" title="Kilkenny">Kilkenny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ballinasloe" title="Ballinasloe">Ballinasloe</a> in the early 19th century. In the 1830s, the game began to spread; many of the clubs which were founded in the following 30&#160;years are still in existence today.<sup id="cite_ref-cricinfo_history_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricinfo_history-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The first Irish national team played in 1855 against The Gentlemen of England in Dublin. In the 1850s, the Englishman Charles Lawrence was responsible for developing the game in Ireland through his coaching.<sup id="cite_ref-cricinfo_history_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricinfo_history-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the 1850s and 1860s, Ireland was visited for the first time by touring professional teams. Ireland\'s first match against <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">Marylebone Cricket Club</a> (the M.C.C.) was in 1858.<sup id="cite_ref-cricinfo_history_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricinfo_history-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The game gained popularity until the early 1880s. The land war in the 1880s resulting from the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Land_Commission" title="Irish Land Commission">Irish Land Commission</a> and a ban on playing "foreign" games, in practice, British, by the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> set back the spread of cricket. The ban was lifted in 1970, and before then anyone playing foreign games,  such as cricket was banned from the Irish games such as <a href="/wiki/Hurling" title="Hurling">hurling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a>. Irish teams toured Canada and the USA in 1879, 1888, 1892, and 1909. On top of this, Ireland defeated a touring South African side in 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-cricinfo_history_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricinfo_history-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Their first match with <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class</a> status was played on 19 May 1902 against a London County side including <a href="/wiki/W.G._Grace" class="mw-redirect" title="W.G. Grace">W.G. Grace</a>. The Irish, captained by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Tim_O%27Brien,_3rd_Baronet" title="Sir Tim O&#39;Brien, 3rd Baronet">Sir Tim O\'Brien</a>, won convincingly by <a href="/wiki/The_result_in_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="The result in cricket">238 runs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_1993">Before 1993</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Before 1993">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After the 1902 tour of England, where four matches yielded one win, two draws and one loss, Ireland did not play first-class cricket again for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Although the team had lost to the South Africans in 1894&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Ireland\'s first match against a Test-playing nation&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 Ireland defeated South Africa in 1904; it was the team\'s first victory against a Test side.<sup id="cite_ref-Irish_timeline_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irish_timeline-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 1909, the first annual first-class match between Ireland and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotland cricket team">Scotland</a> was held, and an annual match against the <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">MCC</a> was arranged from 1924 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-cricinfo_history_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricinfo_history-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Irish played yearly first-class matches with the Scots, only interrupted by world wars, until 1999, but all their other cricket depended upon touring international sides finding it convenient to include a visit to Ireland in their schedules. However, Ireland sometimes surprised <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test</a> nations on these occasions, beating the <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indian cricket team">West Indies</a> by 60 runs in a three-day match in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> in 1928, for example; it was Ireland\'s first match against the West Indies.<sup id="cite_ref-Irish_timeline_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irish_timeline-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 1969, in a match played at <a href="/wiki/Sion_Mills" title="Sion Mills">Sion Mills</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Tyrone" title="County Tyrone">County Tyrone</a>, the team defeated a West Indian side including <a href="/wiki/Clive_Lloyd" title="Clive Lloyd">Clive Lloyd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Walcott" title="Clyde Walcott">Clyde Walcott</a> by nine wickets, after bowling them out for 25.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> This was the last time Ireland defeated a touring side until 2003, when they beat <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwean_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwean cricket team">Zimbabwe</a> by ten wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Scots and the Irish were mostly competing with <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Sri Lankan cricket team">Sri Lanka</a> for the title as the best non-Test nation at the time&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 indeed, Ireland drew with Sri Lanka in a rain-hit first-class match in 1979, Ireland scoring a total of 341 for 7 in two innings, while Sri Lanka made 288 for 6 in one innings. Ireland, along with Scotland and the Netherlands, has at times played in competitions for <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_First_Class_Cricket_Counties" class="mw-redirect" title="List of English First Class Cricket Counties">English county cricket sides</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Benson_%26_Hedges_Cup" title="Benson &amp; Hedges Cup">Benson &amp; Hedges Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Friends_Provident_Trophy" title="Friends Provident Trophy">Friends Provident Trophy</a> (previously the <a href="/wiki/C%26G_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="C&amp;G Trophy">C&amp;G Trophy</a>). Since there is no nationality restriction in county cricket, non-Irish people were allowed to compete for Ireland in these matches. For example, <a href="/wiki/Hansie_Cronje" title="Hansie Cronje">Hansie Cronje</a> of South Africa played for Ireland in 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> as did New Zealander <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Ryder" title="Jesse Ryder">Jesse Ryder</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Associate_member_.281993.E2.80.932007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Associate_member_(1993\xe2\x80\x932007)">Associate member (1993\xe2\x80\x932007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Associate member (1993\xe2\x80\x932007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Ireland joined the ICC as an <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members#Associate_Members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">Associate member</a> in 1993, a year before Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> This meant Ireland could play in the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="ICC Trophy">ICC Trophy</a> for the first time in 1994, and they finished seventh in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Three years later they progressed to the semi-finals of the competition but lost the third place play-off with Scotland, thus missing a place at the <a href="/wiki/1999_cricket_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 cricket World Cup">1999 cricket World Cup</a>. Ireland finished eighth in the 2001 tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> After this, <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Birrell" title="Adrian Birrell">Adrian Birrell</a> was hired as coach.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:100_1795_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/100_1795_%282%29.jpg/170px-100_1795_%282%29.jpg" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/100_1795_%282%29.jpg/255px-100_1795_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/100_1795_%282%29.jpg/340px-100_1795_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1260" data-file-height="1560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:100_1795_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ireland playing against <a href="/wiki/Essex_County_Cricket_Club" title="Essex County Cricket Club">Essex</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Friends_Provident_Trophy" title="Friends Provident Trophy">Friends Provident Trophy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Clontarf_Cricket_Club_Ground" title="Clontarf Cricket Club Ground">Clontarf</a> in 2007.</div></div></div>\n<p>With the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="ICC Intercontinental Cup">ICC Intercontinental Cup</a> in 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Ireland had a chance to play first-class on a regular basis. After failing to progress beyond the group stages in the 2004 <a href="/wiki/2004_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2004 ICC Intercontinental Cup">competition</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Ireland won their first Cup title in <a href="/wiki/2005_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2005 ICC Intercontinental Cup">October 2005</a> with a six-wicket win over Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2005_ICC_Trophy" title="2005 ICC Trophy">2005 ICC Trophy</a>, which was hosted in Ireland&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the group stages in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, the final stages in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 saw the Irish make the final, which they lost to Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Though Ireland were runners-up, they had secured their place at the 2007 World Cup as well as an extra $500,000 over the next four years from the ICC to encourage development of Irish cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-Edward_Craig_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edward_Craig-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> They also gained official ODI status.<sup id="cite_ref-Edward_Craig_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edward_Craig-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ireland\'s inaugural ODI was played in front of a full house of 7,500&#160;spectators at <a href="/wiki/Stormont_(cricket_ground)" title="Stormont (cricket ground)">Stormont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, on 13 June 2006 against England. It was the first time Ireland had played the full England side. Though Ireland lost by 38&#160;runs, they were praised by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Strauss" title="Andrew Strauss">Andrew Strauss</a>, England\'s stand-in captain.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%; clear:both">\n<table style="float:left; width:15%; table-layout:fixed; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div style="text-align:right"> 13 June 2006    <br /><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://m.espncricinfo.com/engvireland/engine/current/match/225171.html">[1]</a> </small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; width:53%; table-layout:fixed; text-align:center; border-style:none">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td style="width:47%; text-align:right; border-style:none"><div><b><a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/23px-Flag_of_England.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/35px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Flag_of_England.svg/46px-Flag_of_England.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="480" /></span></b><br />301/7 (50 overs)</div>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; border-style:none"><div><b>v</b></div>\n</td>\n<td style="width:47%; text-align:left; border-style:none"><div><b><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland"><img alt="Ireland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/23px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/35px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/45px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> Ireland</b><br />263/9 (50 overs)</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td style="text-align:right; border-style:none"><div><small><a href="/wiki/Marcus_Trescothick" title="Marcus Trescothick">Marcus Trescothick</a> 113 (114) <br /><a href="/wiki/Dave_Langford-Smith" title="Dave Langford-Smith">Dave Langford-Smith</a> 3/63 (10 overs)</small></div>\n</td>\n<td style="border-style:none">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left; border-style:none"><div><small><a href="/wiki/Andre_Botha_(cricketer)" title="Andre Botha (cricketer)">Andre Botha</a> 52 (89) <br /><a href="/wiki/Steve_Harmison" title="Steve Harmison">Steve Harmison</a> 3/58 (10 overs)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:right; width:32%; overflow:hidden; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div><b>England won by 38 runs</b><small><br /> <a href="/wiki/Stormont_(cricket_ground)" title="Stormont (cricket ground)">Stormont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> <br />Umpires: <a href="/wiki/Roger_Dill" title="Roger Dill">Roger Dill</a> (BER) and <a href="/wiki/DB_Hair" class="mw-redirect" title="DB Hair">DB Hair</a> (AUS) <br />Player of the match: <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Trescothick" title="Marcus Trescothick">Marcus Trescothick</a> (Eng)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both">\n<ul><li><i>England won the toss and elected to bat.</i></li>\n<li><i>First ever ODI match for Ireland.</i></li></ul></div>\n</div>\n<p>August saw them participate in Division One of the European Championship, against Denmark, <a href="/wiki/Italian_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian cricket team">Italy</a>, the Netherlands and Scotland. The games against the Netherlands and Scotland had ODI status. In the tournament, and what was the team\'s second ODI, Ireland recorded their first ODI win, beating fellow Associates Scotland by 85&#160;runs after man-of-the-match Eoin Morgan made 99.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Although the match against the Netherlands was a no-result, Ireland won the European Championship title.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Ireland\'s second Intercontinental Cup title came in the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Intercontinental_Cup#2006\xe2\x80\x932007_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="ICC Intercontinental Cup">2006\xe2\x80\x932007 competition</a>. They faced Canada in the final and won by an innings and 115 runs, the four-day match concluding within two days. This made Ireland the first team to successfully defend the Continental Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the 2006 season, the C&amp;G Trophy was reorganised to include a round-robin stage instead of being entirely knock-out. Whereas Ireland had only one match guaranteed in the tournament before, they now had more fixtures against English county sides. Ireland recorded one win in their nine matches.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Ireland participated in the competition until it was restructured again in 2009. In that time they played 25 matches and won two.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The latter of those victories was against <a href="/wiki/Worcestershire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Worcestershire County Cricket Club">Worcestershire</a>; in that match Ireland bowled Worcestershire out for 58, which was their lowest ever one-day total. It was the first time that Ireland had bowled out a county for less than 100.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Ireland were invited to participate in the reformatted competition from 2010 onwards, but chose not to do so, and instead focused their limited financial resources on international cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="One_Day_International_status_.282007.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="One_Day_International_status_(2007\xe2\x80\x93present)">One Day International status (2007\xe2\x80\x93present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: One Day International status (2007\xe2\x80\x93present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At the start of 2007, Ireland saw more than three months of almost constant cricket. First was a visit to Kenya, where they took part in <a href="/wiki/2007_ICC_World_Cricket_League_Division_One" title="2007 ICC World Cricket League Division One">Division One</a> of the <a href="/wiki/ICC_World_Cricket_League" class="mw-redirect" title="ICC World Cricket League">ICC World Cricket League</a>. They finished fifth in the league after four narrow defeats, and Kenya won the league.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Before the World Cup, the team participated in a high-performance camp in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-tough_at_the_top_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tough_at_the_top-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Ireland\'s performance in their inaugural World Cup in the <a href="/wiki/Ireland_at_the_Cricket_World_Cup" title="Ireland at the Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a> took many pundits by surprise. In their first game, on 15 March, they tied with <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwean_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwean cricket team">Zimbabwe</a>, primarily thanks to Ireland\'s first ever World Cup century by man-of-the-match <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Bray_(cricketer)" title="Jeremy Bray (cricketer)">Jeremy Bray</a> and economical bowling in the final overs by Trent Johnston and Andre Botha.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In their second match, played on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Day" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Day">Saint Patrick\'s Day</a>, they beat the fourth-ranked team in the world, <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani cricket team">Pakistan</a>, by three wickets, thus knocking Pakistan out of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%; clear:both">\n<table style="float:left; width:15%; table-layout:fixed; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div style="text-align:right"> 17 March 2007    <br /><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.espncricinfo.com/ci/engine/match/247465.html">Scorecard</a> </small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; width:53%; table-layout:fixed; text-align:center; border-style:none">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td style="width:47%; text-align:right; border-style:none"><div><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Pakistan_national_cricket_team" title="Pakistan national cricket team">Pakistan</a></b><br />132 (45.4 overs)</div>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; border-style:none"><div><b>v</b></div>\n</td>\n<td style="width:47%; text-align:left; border-style:none"><div><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/23px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/35px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/45px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Ireland</a></b><br />133/7 (41.4 overs)</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td style="text-align:right; border-style:none"><div><small><a href="/wiki/Kamran_Akmal" title="Kamran Akmal">Kamran Akmal</a> 27 (47) <br /><a href="/wiki/Boyd_Rankin" title="Boyd Rankin">Boyd Rankin</a> 3/32 (9 overs)</small></div>\n</td>\n<td style="border-style:none">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left; border-style:none"><div><small><a href="/wiki/Niall_O%27Brien_(cricketer)" title="Niall O&#39;Brien (cricketer)">Niall O\'Brien</a> 72 (107) <br /><a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Sami" title="Mohammad Sami">Mohammad Sami</a> 3/29 (10 overs)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:right; width:32%; overflow:hidden; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div><b>Ireland won by 3 wickets (<a href="/wiki/Duckworth-Lewis" class="mw-redirect" title="Duckworth-Lewis">D/L method</a>)</b><small><br /> <a href="/wiki/Sabina_Park" title="Sabina Park">Sabina Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> <br />Umpires: <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bowden" title="Billy Bowden">Billy Bowden</a> (NZ) and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Jerling" title="Brian Jerling">Brian Jerling</a> (SA) <br />Player of the match: <a href="/wiki/Niall_O%27Brien_(cricketer)" title="Niall O&#39;Brien (cricketer)">Niall O\'Brien</a> (Ire)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both"> \n<ul><li><i>Rain and bad light reduced Ireland\'s target to 133 from 47 overs.</i> </li></ul></div>\n</div>\n<p>These two results were enough to advance Ireland to the Super 8 stage of the tournament. In their final group stage game, the West Indies beat them by eight wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In the Super 8 stage, they lost their four matches against England, South Africa, New Zealand, Australia, and Sri Lanka,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">that\'s five</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> but recorded a 74-run victory against Test playing nation <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_national_cricket_team" title="Bangladesh national cricket team">Bangladesh</a>, the 9th ranked team in the world. The team received a heroes\' welcome in Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the World Cup, former West Indies cricketer <a href="/wiki/Phil_Simmons" title="Phil Simmons">Phil Simmons</a> took over the role of coach from Birrell.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indian_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian cricket team">India</a> were scheduled to play <a href="/wiki/South_African_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="South African cricket team">South Africa</a> in a series of One Day Internationals in Ireland in June 2007. Ireland also played one-off matches at Stormont against the two teams. Missing several players from their World Cup squad, Ireland lost both games.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Ireland hosted a <a href="/wiki/Quadrangular_Series_in_Ireland_in_2007" title="Quadrangular Series in Ireland in 2007">quadrangular tournament in Dublin and Belfast</a> in July involving the West Indies, the Netherlands, and Scotland. Ireland and the West Indies both won their games against Scotland and the Netherlands with their direct encounter ending in <a href="/wiki/The_result_in_cricket#No_result" class="mw-redirect" title="The result in cricket">no result</a> due to rain. The West Indies won the tournament because of a bonus point won against the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Trent Johnston stepped down as captain and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/William_Porterfield" title="William Porterfield">William Porterfield</a> in March 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2007\xe2\x80\x9308 ICC Intercontinental Cup">2007\xe2\x80\x9308 ICC Intercontinental Cup</a> began in June, with Ireland playing their first match in August. In November 2008, the team\'s campaign ended. After finishing second in the round-robin stage of the competition, Ireland faced <a href="/wiki/Namibia_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Namibia cricket team">Namibia</a> in the final. Ireland won by nine wickets, securing their third consecutive Intercontinental Cup title.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In March 2008 Ireland toured Bangladesh, playing three ODIs against the hosts and losing all of them.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In July, Ireland played a <a href="/wiki/2008_Associates_Tri-Series_in_Scotland" title="2008 Associates Tri-Series in Scotland">tri-series</a> against New Zealand and Scotland in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> but lost both matches.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg/220px-Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg/330px-Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg/440px-Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="796" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_vs_Pakistan2_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ireland playing against Pakistan at the Kennington Oval during the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009 T20 World Cup</a>. <a href="/wiki/Niall_O%27Brien_(cricketer)" title="Niall O&#39;Brien (cricketer)">Niall O\'Brien</a> is keeping wicket whilst and <a href="/wiki/Trent_Johnston" title="Trent Johnston">Trent Johnston</a> is the fielder.</div></div></div>\n<p>Reigning champions Ireland hosted the <a href="/wiki/European_Cricket_Championship" title="European Cricket Championship">European Cricket Championship</a> (Division One) in late July and they won their third European title, winning every match, including the decisive encounter against Scotland by seven wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In early August, Ireland hosted five other Associate nations at the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20_Qualifier" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20 Qualifier">2009 ICC World Twenty20 Qualifier</a> in Belfast; this was Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_International" title="Twenty20 International">Twenty20 International</a> debut. Ireland would have faced the Netherlands in the final, however the match was rained off and the teams shared the trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> By getting to the final of the tournament, Ireland qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009 ICC World Twenty20</a> in England in June 2009. Later in August, Ireland were due to play three ODIs at home against Kenya. Ireland won the first game, the second game could not be finished due to rain and the last match was completely washed out.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In October, the team visited Kenya for a <a href="/wiki/2008_Associates_Tri-Series_in_Kenya" title="2008 Associates Tri-Series in Kenya">tri-series of ODIs</a> with the hosts and Zimbabwe. Only two of Ireland\'s four games in the round-robin stage could be played, the others were rained off. Ireland lost their first match to Zimbabwe,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> but won their second against Kenya, though they failed to qualify for the final.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the run-up to the 2009 ICC World Twenty20, Ireland were deprived of batsman <a href="/wiki/Eoin_Morgan" title="Eoin Morgan">Eoin Morgan</a>, similarly to <a href="/wiki/Ed_Joyce" title="Ed Joyce">Ed Joyce</a> several years earlier, who was selected to play for England, making him ineligible to play for Ireland again.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Ireland played their first Twenty20 International against a full ICC member side on 8 June 2009 and in their opening match of the tournament defeated Bangladesh by four wickets and knocked them out of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Ireland progressed to the second stage of the competition. They were grouped with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_cricket_team" title="New Zealand national cricket team">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_national_cricket_team" title="Pakistan national cricket team">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team" title="Sri Lanka national cricket team">Sri Lanka</a> and lost all three of their matches. In 2009, Ireland played nine ODIs, winning the seven they played against Associate nations, losing their only match against a Test team (England), and one match was abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ireland played 17 One Day Internationals in 2010, winning 11 (including a victory over Bangladesh) and losing six.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Ireland were knocked out of the <a href="/wiki/2010_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2010 ICC World Twenty20">2010 ICC World Twenty20</a>, hosted by South Africa in April and May, after being beaten by the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a> and a washed out match against England.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Porterfield,_2013_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Porterfield%2C_2013_%281%29.jpg/220px-Porterfield%2C_2013_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Porterfield%2C_2013_%281%29.jpg/330px-Porterfield%2C_2013_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Porterfield%2C_2013_%281%29.jpg/440px-Porterfield%2C_2013_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Porterfield,_2013_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Captain William Porterfield batting against England during <a href="/wiki/Malahide_Cricket_Club_Ground" title="Malahide Cricket Club Ground">Malahide Cricket Club Ground</a>\'s inaugural ODI in 2013.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ireland_at_the_Cricket_World_Cup" title="Ireland at the Cricket World Cup">2011 Cricket World Cup</a> was held between February and March and hosted by Bangladesh, India and Sri Lanka. Though Ireland did not progress beyond the first round they secured a historic victory against England.<sup id="cite_ref-2011review_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011review-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Ireland beat England by 3 wickets with <a href="/wiki/Kevin_O%27Brien_(cricketer)" title="Kevin O&#39;Brien (cricketer)">Kevin O\'Brien</a> hitting the fastest century in World Cup history, managing the feat in just 50&#160;balls.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In passing England\'s total of 327 for victory, Ireland broke the record for the highest successful run chase in the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%; clear:both">\n<table style="float:left; width:15%; table-layout:fixed; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div style="text-align:right"> 2 March 2011    <br /><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.espncricinfo.com/icc_cricket_worldcup2011/engine/match/433572.html">Scorecard</a> </small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; width:32%; overflow:hidden; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div><b>Ireland won by 3 wickets</b><small><br /> <a href="/wiki/M_Chinnaswamy_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="M Chinnaswamy Stadium">M Chinnaswamy Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a> <br />Umpires: <a href="/wiki/Aleem_Dar" title="Aleem Dar">Aleem Dar</a> (Pak) and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bowden" title="Billy Bowden">Billy Bowden</a> (NZ) <br />Player of the match: <a href="/wiki/Kevin_O%27Brien_(cricketer)" title="Kevin O&#39;Brien (cricketer)">Kevin O\'Brien</a> (Ire)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both">\n<ul><li><i>England won the toss and elected to bat.</i>  </li></ul></div>\n</div>\n<p>Shortly after the tournament ended, the ICC announced that the World Cups in 2015 and 2019 would contain ten teams; the Associate countries, who were most likely to miss out in a tournament with fewer teams strongly objected, and, led by Ireland, urged the ICC to reconsider. In June the decision was reversed.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> After the World Cup Ireland played Pakistan, England, and Scotland in ODIs but lost each match.<sup id="cite_ref-2011review_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011review-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A further ODI against Sri Lanka was rained off. In all, Ireland played 12&#160;ODIs in 2011, winning four.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ireland qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2015 Cricket World Cup">2015 Cricket World Cup</a>, and were promoted to the ICC ODI Championship, leaving the World Cricket League, but not the ICC Intercontinental Cup. In their first match of the World Cup, Ireland defeated the West Indies by 4 wickets, chasing down 304 runs with 25 balls to spare.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%; clear:both">\n<table style="float:left; width:15%; table-layout:fixed; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div style="text-align:right"> <span id="match5"></span> 16 February    <br /><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.espncricinfo.com/ci/engine/match/656407.html">Scorecard</a> </small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; width:53%; table-layout:fixed; text-align:center; border-style:none">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td style="width:47%; text-align:right; border-style:none"><div><b><a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/WestIndiesCricketFlagPre1999.svg/23px-WestIndiesCricketFlagPre1999.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/WestIndiesCricketFlagPre1999.svg/35px-WestIndiesCricketFlagPre1999.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/WestIndiesCricketFlagPre1999.svg/46px-WestIndiesCricketFlagPre1999.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="309" /></span></b><br />304/7 (50 overs)</div>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; border-style:none"><div><b>v</b></div>\n</td>\n<td style="width:47%; text-align:left; border-style:none"><div><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/23px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/35px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/45px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Ireland</a></b><br />307/6 (45.5 overs)</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td style="text-align:right; border-style:none"><div><small><a href="/wiki/Lendl_Simmons" title="Lendl Simmons">Lendl Simmons</a> 102 (84) <br /><a href="/wiki/George_Dockrell" title="George Dockrell">George Dockrell</a> 3/50 (10 overs)</small></div>\n</td>\n<td style="border-style:none">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left; border-style:none"><div><small><a href="/wiki/Paul_Stirling" title="Paul Stirling">Paul Stirling</a> 92 (84) <br /><a href="/wiki/Jerome_Taylor" title="Jerome Taylor">Jerome Taylor</a> 3/71 (8.5 overs)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:right; width:32%; overflow:hidden; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div><b>Ireland won by 4 wickets</b><small><br /> <a href="/wiki/Saxton_Oval" title="Saxton Oval">Saxton Oval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelson,_New_Zealand" title="Nelson, New Zealand">Nelson</a> <br />Umpires: <a href="/wiki/Richard_Illingworth" title="Richard Illingworth">Richard Illingworth</a> (Eng) and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Oxenford" title="Bruce Oxenford">Bruce Oxenford</a> (Aus) <br />Player of the match: <a href="/wiki/Paul_Stirling" title="Paul Stirling">Paul Stirling</a> (Ire)</small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both">\n<ul><li><i>Ireland won the toss and elected to field.</i>  </li></ul></div>\n</div>\n<p>In their second match they beat the United Arab Emirates by two wickets with four balls to spare; the target was 279. Out of only five successful World Cup chases of 300 runs or more, Ireland have provided three.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, Ireland played in its first <a href="/wiki/Afghan_cricket_team_in_Ireland_in_2016" title="Afghan cricket team in Ireland in 2016">five-match ODI series against Afghanistan</a> which ended 2-2 with the first ODI being washed out. In September, Ireland toured South Africa for <a href="/wiki/Irish_cricket_team_in_South_Africa_in_2016-17" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish cricket team in South Africa in 2016-17">a one match ODI series against Australia and the hosts</a> but lost both games. At the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">ICC</a>\'s board meeting in October, Ireland was awarded <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class</a> status for its domestic competition, the Inter-Provincial Championship.\nIn May 2017, Ireland travelled to England to play a <a href="/wiki/Irish_cricket_team_in_England_in_2017" title="Irish cricket team in England in 2017">two-match ODI series</a> for the first time, though they ended up losing both games.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Test_status_.282017.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Test_status_(2017\xe2\x80\x93present)">Test status (2017\xe2\x80\x93present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Test status (2017\xe2\x80\x93present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In January 2012 Cricket Ireland chief executive Warren Deutrom publicly declared Ireland\'s ambition to play <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test cricket</a> by 2020. Their desire to achieve Test status was in part to stem the tide of Irish players using residency rules to switch to England for the opportunity to play Test cricket. Deutrom outlined the ambition as he unveiled the new strategic plan for Irish cricket to 2015. The plan set out a series of stretching goals including increasing the number of participants in the game to 50,000, setting a target of reaching 8th in the World rankings, establishing a domestic first-class cricket structure, and reinforcing cricket as the fifth most popular team sport in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-CricketIreland2012a_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CricketIreland2012a-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC2012a_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2012a-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Deutrom had already sent a letter to the ICC in 2009 stating his board\'s intention to apply for Full Membership&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 a potential pathway to Test cricket&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 and to seek clarification on the process.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Former Australian bowler <a href="/wiki/Jason_Gillespie" title="Jason Gillespie">Jason Gillespie</a> said that if Ireland got Test status it "would be huge news in world cricket, and it would be a massive positive story for the world game".<sup id="cite_ref-Gillespie_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillespie-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Following Ireland\'s victory over the West Indies in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2015 Cricket World Cup">2015 Cricket World Cup</a>, former fast bowler <a href="/wiki/Michael_Holding" title="Michael Holding">Michael Holding</a> said that the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> should grant Ireland Test status immediately, saying "they need to be recognised now".<sup id="cite_ref-Holding_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holding-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The ICC said in 2015 that Ireland would be granted Test status in 2019 should they win the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9317_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2015\xe2\x80\x9317 ICC Intercontinental Cup">2015\xe2\x80\x9317 ICC Intercontinental Cup</a> and beat the 10th ranked Test nation in a four-match Test series in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, on 22 June 2017, after more than a decade of playing top-class international cricket, full ICC membership was granted to Ireland (along with Afghanistan) at an ICC meeting in London, thus making them the eleventh Test cricket team.<sup id="cite_ref-Afghanistan_Ireland_full_test_status_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Afghanistan_Ireland_full_test_status-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In October 2017, the ICC announced that Ireland\'s first Test match would be at home <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_cricket_team_in_Ireland_in_2018" title="Pakistani cricket team in Ireland in 2018">against Pakistan</a> in May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-confirm_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-confirm-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CI1st_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CI1st-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Ireland are scheduled to play a four-day Test match against England at <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s" title="Lord&#39;s">Lord\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Irish_cricket_team_in_England_in_2019" title="Irish cricket team in England in 2019">in July 2019</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lord&#39;s_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lord&#39;s-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Future_Tours_Programme" title="ICC Future Tours Programme">ICC Future Tours Programme</a> for 2019\xe2\x80\x9323, Ireland are scheduled to play sixteen Tests.<sup id="cite_ref-IreFTP_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IreFTP-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%;">\n<table style="float:left; width:15%; table-layout:fixed; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border-style:none"><div style="text-align:right">11\xe2\x80\x9315 May 2018<sup id="cite_ref-Day_1_lost_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Day_1_lost-89">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup>   <br /><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.espncricinfo.com/ci/engine/match/1127284.html">Scorecard</a> </small></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; light and rain.</i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Balbirnie" title="Andrew Balbirnie">Andrew Balbirnie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Joyce" title="Ed Joyce">Ed Joyce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyrone_Kane" href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governing_body">Governing body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governing body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Irish_Cricket_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Cricket Union">Irish Cricket Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/220px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/330px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg/440px-Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_Ireland_flag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the Irish team</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_Cricket_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Cricket Union">Irish Cricket Union</a> (ICU)&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the governing body of Irish cricket&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 was officially founded in 1923, although its predecessor had been active since 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-cricinfo_history_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricinfo_history-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In common with a number of other Ireland sporting governing bodies, the Union was formed to represent cricket throughout the island of Ireland, rather than just the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>. In common with its counterparts for <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rugby_Football_Union" title="Irish Rugby Football Union">rugby union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irish_Hockey_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Hockey Association">field hockey</a>, the Union therefore does not use the <a href="/wiki/Irish_tricolor" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish tricolor">Irish tricolor</a>, but instead employs its own flag, which is used by such bodies as the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> to represent the team and in ICC tournaments; "<a href="/wiki/Ireland%27s_Call" title="Ireland&#39;s Call">Ireland\'s Call</a>" is used as the national anthem.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, the ICU announced major changes to bring it into line with the main cricket governing bodies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">what were they?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-major_changes_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-major_changes-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> After the World Cup, Irish cricket had poor results in the 2007 Friends Provident Trophy, as many players were unavailable. The Irish cricket team was an amateur side and most of the players had full-time jobs with commitments conflicting with cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-tough_at_the_top_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tough_at_the_top-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Warren Deutrom, the chief executive of the ICU, has stated that it wants to "seek actively to place Irish players into top-level cricket, by developing relationships with [especially] county cricket which will incorporate appropriate player release for Irish international duty, and feeder systems for developing Irish cricketers".<sup id="cite_ref-major_changes_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-major_changes-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The reorganised ICU sought closer links with the English county teams, to encourage the development of age group cricket, and to introduce a professional element into the Irish game. They also want to take the Ireland cricket team on winter tours more often.<sup id="cite_ref-major_changes_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-major_changes-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an attempt to prevent the game losing players to counties or other commitments such as jobs, it was suggested that central contracts should be introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> This was done in June 2009, with the first two going to <a href="/wiki/Trent_Johnston" title="Trent Johnston">Trent Johnston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Cusack" title="Alex Cusack">Alex Cusack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The number of full-time contracts was expanded to six in January 2010 with support for a further nine players; the contracts were split into three categories.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In January 2012 the number of contracts was increased to 23, and coach Phil Simmons highlighted the process of becoming professional as an important factor in the team\'s success.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tournament_history">Tournament history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tournament history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Cup">World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_staff">Playing staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ireland_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Playing staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This lists all the active players who have played for Ireland in the past year (since 4 September 2017) and the forms in which they have played, or any players (in italics) outside this criteria who have been selected in the team\'s most recent squad. In addition, it includes all 20 players contracted by <a href="/wiki/Cricket_Ireland" title="Cricket Ireland">Cricket Ireland</a> in January 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-2018_contracts_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_contracts-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> apart from <a href="/wiki/Ed_Joyce" title="Ed Joyce">Ed Joyce</a> who retired from professional cricket in May
